The Washington Post <a href=\"https:\/\/www.washingtonpost.com\/nation\/2019\/07\/26\/it-snuck-up-us-city-killer-asteroid-just-missed-earth-scientists-almost-didnt-detect-it-time\/\" target=\"_blank\">reported<\/a>\u00a0that scientists apparently had no idea it was coming.<\/p><p>Asteroid 2019 OK came hurtling toward Earth at a speed of nearly 15 miles a second, before flying past. According to <a href=\"https:\/\/ssd.jpl.nasa.gov\/sbdb.cgi?sstr=2019%20OK;old=0;orb=1;cov=0;log=0;cad=0#orb\" target=\"_blank\">NASA<\/a>, it was about 45,000 miles from Earth on Thursday.<\/p><p>\"It would have hit with over 30 times the energy of the atomic blast at Hiroshima,\" astronomer professor Alan Duffy told the Sydney Morning Herald. Duffy called the zooming space rock a \"city killer.\"<\/p><div data-shortcode=\"twitter_tweet\" data-size=\"small\" data-float=\"none\" data-oembed=\"{&quot;author_name&quot;:&quot;ASAS-SN&quot;,&quot;author_url&quot;:&quot;https:\\\/\\\/twitter.com\\\/SuperASASSN&quot;,&quot;cache_age&quot;:&quot;3153600000&quot;,&quot;height&quot;:null,&quot;html&quot;:&quot;&lt;blockquote class=\\&quot;twitter-tweet\\&quot;&gt;&lt;p lang=\\&quot;en\\&quot; dir=\\&quot;ltr\\&quot;&gt;This is the video of the close encounter of Asteroid 2019 OK we have been Twitting all day with the Earth: &lt;a href=\\&quot;https:\\\/\\\/t.co\\\/bjT7uhQJuO\\&quot;&gt;https:\\\/\\\/t.co\\\/bjT7uhQJuO&lt;\\\/a&gt; &lt;a href=\\&quot;https:\\\/\\\/t.co\\\/3e4UyPcdPl\\&quot;&gt;pic.twitter.com\\\/3e4UyPcdPl&lt;\\\/a&gt;&lt;\\\/p&gt;&amp;mdash; ASAS-SN (@SuperASASSN) &lt;a href=\\&quot;https:\\\/\\\/twitter.com\\\/SuperASASSN\\\/status\\\/1154190931509350401?ref_src=twsrc^tfw\\&quot;&gt;July 25, 2019&lt;\\\/a&gt;&lt;\\\/blockquote&gt;\\n&quot;,&quot;provider_name&quot;:&quot;Twitter&quot;,&quot;provider_url&quot;:&quot;https:\\\/\\\/twitter.com&quot;,&quot;type&quot;:&quot;rich&quot;,&quot;url&quot;:&quot;https:\\\/\\\/twitter.com\\\/SuperASASSN\\\/status\\\/1154190931509350401&quot;,&quot;version&quot;:&quot;1.0&quot;,&quot;width&quot;:550}\" data-url=\"https:\/\/twitter.com\/SuperASASSN\/status\/1154190931509350401\" data-conversation=\"true\"\/><p>Astronomers say it posed no immediate threat but they admit they had no idea the giant rock was headed our way, because it came from the direction of the sun.<\/p><p>The asteroid, about the size of a large boulder, only became visible a few days ago.<\/p><p>There are 20,000 near-Earth asteroids and they do occasionally make an appearance. In 2013, one slammed into Russia, injuring 1,600 people.\u00a0 \u00a0 \u00a0<\/p><p>At a conference in April, scientists from around the world were asked <span data-shortcode=\"link\" data-asset-type=\"article\" data-uuid=\"9ffd2d24-778b-4a46-9502-5cca279aafdb\" data-slug=\"how-nasa-would-keep-an-asteroid-from-hitting-the-earth-2019-04-30\" data-link-text=\"how to respond\" data-target=\"_blank\" data-href=\"https:\/\/www.cbsnews.com\/news\/how-nasa-would-keep-an-asteroid-from-hitting-the-earth-2019-04-30\/\" data-edition=\"us\">how to respond<\/span>\u00a0to a make-believe scenario in which an asteroid big enough to destroy a major city might be on track to strike the Earth in eight years.<\/p><p>The likely response would be using space ships to give the asteroid a nudge, one scientist said.<\/p><p>\"All we have to do is change its speed a little faster or a little slower so that when it crosses Earth\u0027s orbit, it crosses either in front of us or behind us,\" said Dr. Lori Glaze, director of planetary science at NASA.<\/p><div data-shortcode=\"video\" data-uuid=\"53eb74f2-e1c1-47b5-891c-32904a9a7d04\" data-size=\"medium\" data-float=\"none\"\/><\/body>","alternativeHeadline":"\"City killer\" asteroid misses Earth \u2014 and scientists had no idea","video":{"@context":"https:\/\/schema.org","@type":"VideoObject","mainEntityOfPage":{"@type":"WebPage","@id":"https:\/\/www.cbsnews.com\/video\/dangerous-asteroid-just-missed-hitting-earth\/"},"name":"Dangerous asteroid just missed hitting Earth","description":"Scientists revealed an asteroid dubbed by some as a \"city killer\" came closer to the Earth than the moon this week, the Washington Post reported. HMw5W5O%2FqlAx6nA3OEmPiGr3uebdR4jns6WLrvtfl06Gdgj%2BjpyfUW7rfU0JbicQ1Lgn7AxbyuteVorqJwy5v9zfqAwW0xgbE1KL%2Fa%2FgZCbAbJYaW3oBptnifVENDzdHRW%2BoHvpG3KA0t1Q9PJbXT8Tb26fj9jHlp9WCYExpHumUERTZB8cTGExAnAmaYTnYCIkMgslYzAuLIzeO0wRupogTNcKjxBjRD7D%2F0jMzPBf6WZkYy%2FGKYXzf67u9%2FBw%3D%3D"     </div>
    <div class="player-overlay--draggable-handle"><!-- keep me outside uvp div --></div>

  </div>

    </div>

      </figure><section data-page="1" data-page-hidden="0" data-use-autolinker="true"><p>Scientists revealed an asteroid dubbed by some as a "city killer" came closer to the Earth than the moon this week. The Washington Post <a href="https://www.washingtonpost.com/nation/2019/07/26/it-snuck-up-us-city-killer-asteroid-just-missed-earth-scientists-almost-didnt-detect-it-time/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">reported</a>&nbsp;that scientists apparently had no idea it was coming.</p><div class="ad-wrapper">
  
    
    
<div id="mpu-plus-top-right-rail" data-ad="mpu-plus-top-right-rail" class="ad-mpu-plus-top-right-rail lazyload lazypreload" data-ad-unit='"mpu-plus-top-right-rail"'>
    </div>
</div>
<p>Asteroid 2019 OK came hurtling toward Earth at a speed of nearly 15 miles a second, before flying past. According to <a href="https://ssd.jpl.nasa.gov/sbdb.cgi?sstr=2019%20OK;old=0;orb=1;cov=0;log=0;cad=0#orb" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">NASA</a>, it was about 45,000 miles from Earth on Thursday.</p><p>"It would have hit with over 30 times the energy of the atomic blast at Hiroshima," astronomer professor Alan Duffy told the Sydney Morning Herald. Duffy called the zooming space rock a "city killer."</p><figure class="embed embed--type-twitter-tweet embed--float-none embed--size-small lazyload" data-require="third-party/twitter-widgets" data-require-callback="twitterInit"><div class="embed__content-wrapper">
    <blockquote class="twitter-tweet"><p lang="en" dir="ltr">This is the video of the close encounter of Asteroid 2019 OK we have been Twitting all day with the Earth: <a href="https://t.co/bjT7uhQJuO" rel="nofollow noopener">https://t.co/bjT7uhQJuO</a> <a href="https://t.co/3e4UyPcdPl" rel="nofollow noopener">pic.twitter.com/3e4UyPcdPl</a></p>&mdash; ASAS-SN (@SuperASASSN) <a href="https://twitter.com/SuperASASSN/status/1154190931509350401?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw" rel="nofollow noopener">July 25, 2019</a></blockquote>

  </div>
</figure><p>Astronomers say it posed no immediate threat but they admit they had no idea the giant rock was headed our way, because it came from the direction of the sun.</p>                
                
        <div class="content-recirculation__wrapper ">
            <figure class="content-recirculation">
                <h4 class="content-recirculation__headline">

                <ul>
                                            <li><a href="https://www.cbsnews.com/live-news/garlic-festival-mass-shooting-gilroy-california-victims-suspect-santino-william-legan-live-updates/?intcid=CNI-00-10aaa3b" data-invalid-url-rewritten-http="">California Festival Shooting</a></li>
                                            <li><a href="https://www.cbsnews.com/news/baltimore-reactions-are-swift-after-trump-calls-city-rodent-infested/?intcid=CNI-00-10aaa3b" data-invalid-url-rewritten-http="">Trump Attacks Cummings</a></li>
                                            <li><a href="https://www.cbsnews.com/news/capital-one-data-breach-2019-more-than-100-million-people-applying-for-credit-affected-today-2019-07-29/?intcid=CNI-00-10aaa3b" data-invalid-url-rewritten-http="">Capital One Data Breach</a></li>
                                            <li><a href="https://www.cbsnews.com/news/hot-car-twins-death-1-year-old-twins-puts-spotlight-on-hot-car-dangers/?intcid=CNI-00-10aaa3b" data-invalid-url-rewritten-http="">Hot Car Dangers</a></li>
                                    </ul>
                            </figure>

        </div>
    <p>The asteroid, about the size of a large boulder, only became visible a few days ago.</p><p>There are 20,000 near-Earth asteroids and they do occasionally make an appearance. In 2013, one slammed into Russia, injuring 1,600 people.&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;</p><p>At a conference in April, scientists from around the world were asked <span class="link"><a href="https://www.cbsnews.com/news/how-nasa-would-keep-an-asteroid-from-hitting-the-earth-2019-04-30/" data-invalid-url-rewritten-http="">how to respond</a></span>&nbsp;to a make-believe scenario in which an asteroid big enough to destroy a major city might be on track to strike the Earth in eight years.</p><p>The likely response would be using space ships to give the asteroid a nudge, one scientist said.</p><p>"All we have to do is change its speed a little faster or a little slower so that when it crosses Earth's orbit, it crosses either in front of us or behind us," said Dr. Lori Glaze, director of planetary science at NASA.</p><figure class="embed embed--type-video embed--type-content_video is-video embed--float-none embed--size-medium"><div class="embed__content-wrapper">
      <div class="embed__resizer"></div>

        





    <iframe           NBA star's desperate call for help
      </h4>

      <p class="item__dek">
        Listen to former NBA star Lorenzen Wright&rsquo;s frantic 911 call made on the night in 2010 that he was murdered. Wright was unable to give his name or location as 11 gunshots are heard before the call cuts out. It took days for authorities to learn that it was Wright who made the call.
